<div id="review_1987441936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987441936" />
    <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes"><img alt="aPriL does feral sometimes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478243665p2/3409532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1987441936?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18789578-mythago-wood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=woman-warrier">woman-warrier</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=magical-drama">magical-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=metafiction">metafiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=mysteries-potboilers-thrillers">mysteries-potboilers-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=sword-and-sorcery">sword-and-sorcery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1987441936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11784186491972040758">Most forests today and in the recent past are only a few centuries old or less. But there still remain a few forests which have been on earth for millennia. In these deep dark old places it is rumored beings which can only live in the most ancient impenetrable deep woods can yet be occasionally seen. It is said the mythological creatures of old deep woods need to be placated and bribed with gifts of blood and flesh if you live near such a forest. People also carve magical symbols into the rock a</span>
  <span id="freeText11784186491972040758" style="display:none">Most forests today and in the recent past are only a few centuries old or less. But there still remain a few forests which have been on earth for millennia. In these deep dark old places it is rumored beings which can only live in the most ancient impenetrable deep woods can yet be occasionally seen. It is said the mythological creatures of old deep woods need to be placated and bribed with gifts of blood and flesh if you live near such a forest. People also carve magical symbols into the rock and wood of ancient forests, hoping to magically confine these spirits of Nature away from the homes of people, but some people seek out these dangerous ghosts of rock, tree, mud and flora. Such a one was Steven Huxley's father, George Huxley.<br /><br />Steven never knew what his father was doing in the woods near his parents' house, Oak Lodge. Steven felt abandoned by George, who left for weeks, even months, hiking and camping in the forest next to their house in Herefordshire, England. When George was home, he remained in his study with old books and papers. Jennifer, George's wife, shared in whatever obsessed George, but she became depressed and took her own life. Steven and Christian, George's sons, could not understand why or what their father was pursuing in Mythago Wood. When World War II started, both boys left for Europe to fight in the war. Afterwords, Christian returned to Oak Lodge, while Steven remained with friends in France. Then, George died in 1946, and Christian wrote Steven of a marriage to a Guiwenneth, a beautiful girl. Finally, late in 1947, Steven reluctantly decided to come back to England. <br /><br />His first view of the house surprised him as it was a bit rundown and worn. But when he saw his brother Christian, Steven was shocked. Christian was dirty, thin and nervous. Worse, he smelled horribly, as if he had not bathed in a week. Plus Christian is wearing a long beard! And, where was Christian's wife? Christian doesn't want to talk about it. Then, Christian says, ""I've been going through a few changes, that's all. I've been picking up on the old man's work. Perhaps a bit of his reclusiveness is rubbing off on me, a bit of his detachment.""<br /><br />The next morning, Christian tells Steven he must go into the woods ""Inwards,"", where he disappears with a rucksack for several weeks. Two weeks after Christian hiked into the woods, Steven finds a woman's body buried under the chicken huts....<br /><br />'Mythago Wood' is a beautifully written homage to the traditional Celtic and Welsh fairy tales of creatures living in the deep forests (and Carl Jung's theories: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungian_archetypes">https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungi...</a>). I do not mean the emasculated versions designed for modern Western children - I refer to the more violent and raunchy ancient versions which entertained and terrified hunters and farmers before the Romans invaded England. These fairy tales were myths about imagined (or real) magical tree beings and transformed woodsmen or vegetation god or goddess warriors living in deep forests. Many of these ancient tales are about the mythical Green Man: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Man">https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green...</a>. Another is Sir Gawain and the Green Knight: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sir_Gawain_and_the_Green_Knight">https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sir_G...</a>. Guinevere is also a character which is based on older myths, but she has become gentrified. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guinevere">https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guine...</a>. Druid stories (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Druid">https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Druid</a>), too, figure into the writing of 'Mythago Wood'. <br /><br />Author Robert Holdstock has re-purposed these ancient popular tales into an entirely new and romantic myth with gorgeous poetic writing. If you find walking in the woods peaceful and satisfying, reading this novel brings that experience to the fore, despite the underlying mysteries of blood and sacrifice haunting most ancient forests and Holdstock's Mythago series.<br /><br />A sample of Holdstock's writing:<br /><br />"I followed him inwards, seeking the easiest route between tangles of bracken and nettles, enjoying the heavy stillness. The trees were small, here at the edge, but within a hundred yards they began to show their real age, great gnarled oak trunks, hollow and half-dead, twisting up from the ground, almost groaning beneath the weight of the branches. The ground rose slightly and the tangled undergrowth was broken by weathered, lichen-covered stubs of grey limestone. We passed over the crest and the earth dipped sharply down, and a subtle change came over the woodland. It seemed darker, somehow, more alive, and I noticed that the shrill September bird-sound of the forest edge was replaced, here, by a sporadic mournful song."<br /><br />Oooooh, this is a good read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11784186491972040758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_652507879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/652507879" />
    <a title="Colleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2643370-colleen"><img alt="Colleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472925167p2/2643370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/652507879?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colleen" href="/user/show/2643370-colleen">Colleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2643370-colleen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer652507879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8588777963779812576">While the concept is awesome, I find myself agreeing with those who think this book is just so-so. I won't rehash everything in detail, I'll just hit the main objections:<br/>*There's nothing likeable about any of the characters, all of whom remain ciphers from beginning to end.<br/>*Nobody ever bloody talks to each other in the way that normal folks do when confusion exists, which makes the relationships unbelievable.<br/>*The love story isn't even remotely romantic. He loves that she smells bad and hangs out</span>
  <span id="freeText8588777963779812576" style="display:none">While the concept is awesome, I find myself agreeing with those who think this book is just so-so. I won't rehash everything in detail, I'll just hit the main objections:<br />*There's nothing likeable about any of the characters, all of whom remain ciphers from beginning to end.<br />*Nobody ever bloody talks to each other in the way that normal folks do when confusion exists, which makes the relationships unbelievable.<br />*The love story isn't even remotely romantic. He loves that she smells bad and hangs out in trees. Well all right then.<br />*LOTS of telling and not showing. LOTS of repetitious ideas. Not a whole lot going on for very long stretches. Dad's diaries, our main source for understanding what the heck is going on, are a really big drag.<br />*I couldn't determine whether all the mythical characters were based on actual myths or just made up by the author. I kept wanting Steven to ground us somehow with the less familiar legends, to reassure us that elements of them had indeed passed down through the collective memory of British culture, even if the stories themselves had been lost to the mists of time. After all, Steven had spent months and months in that house with no job and no friends--why NOT study the old legends, familiarize himself (and us) with what lived in the woods? In fact, that is ultimately my chief objection. I wanted Steven to meet Robin Hood and Arthur and Merlin and other familiar characters, and then afterward get drawn into the more obscure legends. Perhaps he might've taken the time to learn other eras' languages (note that it was incumbent upon Guinneth to learn modern English)and so learn something new about the legends. Instead, the denizens of the wood exist in a whirling, aggressive, noncommunicative mishmash.<br />*Finally, the whole Harry Keeton aspect to the story was perfectly bizarre. Real people would've had an actual discussion after the plane ride. Harry would have revealed his experience in France and his interest in photographing that wood. Steven would have explained what he knows about the woods. Instead, when things happen everyone simply takes them for granted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8588777963779812576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8029217351049486600">This book really glued me to my seat. I remember reading it one time when I was going to Hong Kong.<br/><br/>Going to HK from Shenzhen was an affair. You had to cross the border and take buses and trains and stand in line a lot. This book was really good, and the suspense is wonderful.<br/><br/>If you want a good stand-alone fantasy book I recommend it. I bought the second book (can't remember it's name) but I never got around to reading it.<br/><br/>Would I read it again? I think I would if I had to travel in HK again.</span>

<div id="review_926653611" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926653611" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/926653611?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=the-numinous-book-club">the-numinous-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926653611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10312154949362186886">Totally original, immersive novel. Mythago Wood started out so normal and moved sequentially to the fantastic and magical that you actually believe it. Loved this.<br/><br/>The idea of archetypes coming alive and inhabiting a world "within" our own is very kabballistic and fascinating. I honestly didn't see the twists and turns that happened in this. What fun it was it read an unpredictable novel. It was terrifying at times and wonderful. I highly recommend this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2160748586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2160748586" />
    <a title="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22985424-sad-sunday-if-i-say-it-s-bad-it-s-bad"><img alt="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544800600p2/22985424.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" href="/user/show/22985424-sad-sunday-if-i-say-it-s-bad-it-s-bad">Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2160748586" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5642729289950155156">Uh, this one is tricky. Can I just say that two super-English brothers got so high in the house on the Prairies that a nearby forest suddenly turned into a Wonderland? <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528964716ra/25775762.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>For me Mythago Wood has the vibe of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25350.Out_of_the_Silent_Planet__Space_Trilogy___1_' title='Out of the Silent Planet (Space Trilogy, #1) by C.S. Lewis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Out of the Silent Planet</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7234875.The_Little_Stranger' title='The Little Stranger by Sarah Waters' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Little Stranger</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/331256.Roadside_Picnic' title='Roadside Picnic by Arkady Strugatsky' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roadside Picnic</a>.   <span id="freeText5642729289950155156" style="display:none">Uh, this one is tricky. Can I just say that two super-English brothers got so high in the house on the Prairies that a nearby forest suddenly turned into a Wonderland? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528964716ra/25775762.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For me Mythago Wood has the vibe of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25350.Out_of_the_Silent_Planet__Space_Trilogy___1_" title="Out of the Silent Planet (Space Trilogy, #1) by C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">Out of the Silent Planet</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7234875.The_Little_Stranger" title="The Little Stranger by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">The Little Stranger</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/331256.Roadside_Picnic" title="Roadside Picnic by Arkady Strugatsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Roadside Picnic</a>. Somehow I can't call "fantasy". For me it's more of a magical realism. And while author twists the real and the unreal into a nice and flowing tale, sometimes it's hard to really get into the story, because the myths used in the story are very far away from my background. I loved how the lives of characters were entangled with mythagos, but for example the myth of Guinwenneth was too unknown (even if explained in the book) to truly grasp her character and nature.<br><br>Also, I am still a little puzzled who and what exactly is a mythago. But well, I guess it's my own problem, as a reader. I liked the overall idea of myth coming to live in a deep dark forest and it had a great deep dark vibe to it, but sometimes I felt lost between myth, reality, explanation, history, beliefs, superstitions and origins of the characters. But it was dramatic, well-done, deep and kinda interesting. But somehow my rating is still 3*. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5642729289950155156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_84798506" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84798506" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/970762-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204770611p2/970762.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84798506?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/970762-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970762-jim?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi-and-horror">fantasy-sci-fi-and-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970762-jim?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970762-jim?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/970762-jim?shelf=this-sceptred-isle">this-sceptred-isle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84798506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3014170805855619735">I would classify this book as high concept fantasy. Certainly, it is not to everyone's taste. I can sympathize with this, as sometimes I feel like I admire this book more than enjoy it. <br/><br/>Holdstock works through a lot of interesting ideas. The title <i>Mythago Wood</i> refers to a stand of West Midlands primeval forest that, like the TARDIS, is bigger within than without. The forest has an aura that interacts with the mytho-creative aspects of people's minds to produce mythagos, which are expressions of </span>
  <span id="freeText3014170805855619735" style="display:none">I would classify this book as high concept fantasy. Certainly, it is not to everyone's taste. I can sympathize with this, as sometimes I feel like I admire this book more than enjoy it. <br /><br />Holdstock works through a lot of interesting ideas. The title <i>Mythago Wood</i> refers to a stand of West Midlands primeval forest that, like the TARDIS, is bigger within than without. The forest has an aura that interacts with the mytho-creative aspects of people's minds to produce mythagos, which are expressions of mythic archetypes.<br /><br />I have read this book multiple times, and if I have a criticism, it is that the book gets a little lost in its concepts to the detriment of story. The basic plot revolves around two brothers, their distant, obsessive father, and a romantic triangle (quadrangle) involving one of the female mythagos. <br /><br />Holdstock is brilliant at character development, and the ideas he works with are certainly interesting, though pretty familiar to anyone who has read much of the fantasy published since. When it is focused on plot, I think it's great. When it wallows in the concepts, it suffers a bit but is still worth reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3014170805855619735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2192783363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2192783363" />
    <a title="Roxana Chirilă" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21223898-roxana-chiril"><img alt="Roxana Chirilă" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370981378p2/21223898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2192783363?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxana Chirilă" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxana Chirilă" href="/user/show/21223898-roxana-chiril">Roxana Chirilă</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2192783363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1730568767782726158">„“This is the Island where Dreams come true.”<br/>“That's the island I've been looking for this long time,” said one of the sailors. “I reckoned I'd find I was married to Nancy if we landed here.”<br/>“And I'd find Tom alive again,” said another.<br/>“Fools!” said the man, stamping his foot with rage. “That is the sort of talk that brought me here, and I'd better have been drowned or never born. Do you hear what I say? This is where dreams—dreams, do you understand, come to life, come real. Not daydreams: drea</span>
  <span id="freeText1730568767782726158" style="display:none">„“This is the Island where Dreams come true.”<br />“That's the island I've been looking for this long time,” said one of the sailors. “I reckoned I'd find I was married to Nancy if we landed here.”<br />“And I'd find Tom alive again,” said another.<br />“Fools!” said the man, stamping his foot with rage. “That is the sort of talk that brought me here, and I'd better have been drowned or never born. Do you hear what I say? This is where dreams—dreams, do you understand, come to life, come real. Not daydreams: dreams.”<br />There was about half a minute's silence and then, with a great clatter of armour, the whole crew were tumbling down the main hatch as quick as they could and flinging themselves on the oars to row as they had never rowed before;”<br /><br />The above isn't a quote from "Mythago Wood" - it's a quote from C.S. Lewis's "Voyage of the Dawn Trader", a book I read a long time ago, but the dark island of dreams is still something I remember as well as if I'd read about it yesterday. And it sprung to mind while reading this because "Mythago Wood" is about the place where myths come true. And no matter how wonderful that sounds, one has to remember that fairy tales and myths were a lot darker than we tell them now, a lot bloodier, and much more dangerous. It's not all fun and magic, on the contrary.<br /><br />After the second world war, Stephen Huxley returns home from France, expecting to find his brother, Christian, happily married, living in their old family home after the death of their father. When he does, he finds a greatly changed man whose wife has vanished and who now shares their father's obsession with the small wood outside their home. <br /><br />Christian claims that their father discovered mythagos - or incarnations of myths - inside the woods, and that the two of them have seen them as children. Thus, he goes into the wilderness, bidding Stephen to stay behind as he searches for the myths of mankind, created and recreated from the subconscious racial memory of those who come into contact with the woods.<br /><br />Strange things start happening - odd people appearing around Stephen's house, the forest turning him around when he tries to enter it. But the oddest of all is finding Christian's wife buried in a shallow grave next to the chicken coops, while Christian insists she'll return again, since there have been many of her, and there will be many of her again.<br /><br />The story has a strange, mythical horror feel to it, and the atmosphere is wonderfully chilling and eerie. <br /><br />It's hard to explain what I didn't like, but I don't feel like I recognize any mythagos - if they truly are from the depths of the human mind, shouldn't some of them feel more familiar? I'm not so sure about the way characters act and react, either - why is Stephen so madly in love with G., aside from the story demanding him to be? Are these mythagos really myths, or did they spring from these men's subconscious somehow?<br /><br />But otherwise, it's a strange and unusual story and worth a read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1730568767782726158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2192783363">

<div id="review_222339721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222339721" />
    <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma"><img alt="Nandakishore Varma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583648733p2/6237864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222339721?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425087855" href="/book/show/921217.Mythago_Wood">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222339721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15677717594089821993">This is an acclaimed book. The basic premise is the concept of mythagos, which are images from the Jungian collective unconscious, which take corporeal form inside Ryhope Wood. Those who go after the mythagos into the wood are permanently affected.<br/><br/>There is a dreamlike quality to this book which I found endearing at the time of reading - however, much of the story did not stick with me. At the time of reading, I was not much into Joseph Campbell and Jung (that came later), so I was confused with </span>
  <span id="freeText15677717594089821993" style="display:none">This is an acclaimed book. The basic premise is the concept of mythagos, which are images from the Jungian collective unconscious, which take corporeal form inside Ryhope Wood. Those who go after the mythagos into the wood are permanently affected.<br /><br />There is a dreamlike quality to this book which I found endearing at the time of reading - however, much of the story did not stick with me. At the time of reading, I was not much into Joseph Campbell and Jung (that came later), so I was confused with many of the mythopoetic references.<br /><br />So the three stars are entirely subjective. If you are a serious purveyor of literary fantasy, most probably this will thrill you. I think it would be the same case with me on a re-read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15677717594089821993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74232429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer51673832774750894">I wasn't really taken with this book, but my wife (who passed away recently) loved it. I list it here in her honer. Where I found it slightly wandering and lacking focus, she saw beautiful prose. So you might try it. I admit it has a certain "feel" and "voice" it just didn't reach me as it did her.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7Z+Xmn2J7wxsXONFjS+JZuCE/b44LFqsHqAKue3cAexUMX3lncxetEKlKEPCENawfarNpEnmvkYAiY+ASwlOxw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JGtSL+OG0B05RexahRmB3xwYvHZ9QbgIk/ZvXra+vlCdxbhQA8NhpRe8J1zKJt4JgTaMbAyLXOKN3+pnEGvxew==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8049983180556854661">Robert Paul Holdstock was an English novelist and author who is best known for his works of fantasy literature, predominantly in the fantasy subgenre of mythic fiction.<br/><br/>Holdstock's writing was first published in 1968. His science fiction and fantasy works explore philosophical, psychological, anthropological, spiritual, and woodland themes. He has received three BSFA awards and won the World Fantas</span>
  <span id="freeText8049983180556854661" style="display:none">Robert Paul Holdstock was an English novelist and author who is best known for his works of fantasy literature, predominantly in the fantasy subgenre of mythic fiction.<br /><br />Holdstock's writing was first published in 1968. His science fiction and fantasy works explore philosophical, psychological, anthropological, spiritual, and woodland themes. He has received three BSFA awards and won the World Fantasy Award in the category of Best Novel in 1985.<br /><br />Pseudonyms are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1866631.Chris_Carlsen" title="Chris Carlsen" rel="nofollow noopener">Chris Carlsen</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/202194.Robert_Faulcon" title="Robert Faulcon" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Faulcon</a>,Robert Black, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/876045.Steven_Eisler" title="Steven Eisler" rel="nofollow noopener">Steven Eisler</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/159928.Richard_Kirk" title="Richard Kirk" rel="nofollow noopener">Richard Kirk</a>.</span>
